## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through restoring forces, damping, and driving terms. The nonlinearity can appear in any of these contributions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Softening/hardening spring with drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t + c5) (general driven Duffing)
- Nonlinear damping variant: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 + c2 * v**3 (position-dependent and cubic damping)
- Mathieu-type parametric: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (parametrically driven oscillator)
- General cubic system: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v + c4 * x * v**2 (full cubic polynomial in x,v)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (sinusoidal restoring force with damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (linear driven-damped)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (quadratic nonlinearity in restoring force)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — use when system has symmetric potential
- Even-power restoring terms (x²) break symmetry and indicate asymmetric potential wells (Helmholtz-type)
- Velocity-position coupling terms like x²*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-excited oscillators (van der Pol type)
- Periodic time dependence via sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external driving force — look for resonance phenomena
- Negative linear damping (positive coefficient on v) combined with nonlinear damping (x²*v) indicates limit cycle behavior
- If acceleration has no explicit time dependence, the system is autonomous and energy methods apply
- Cubic position terms with sign opposite to linear term indicate Duffing-type hardening (same sign) or softening (opposite sign) spring
- Odd-symmetry in velocity terms (v, v³) preserves time-reversal properties of the conservative part
